<div

<div
class="header
artist_info_header
int-1
clearfix">














<h1
class="hed-1"
title="A
Tribe
Called
Quest"
itemprop="name">A
Tribe
Called
Quest</h1>














<div
class="header_btns">















<div
class="bookmark"
data-musicid="R17149"></div>














</div>













</div>













<div
class="int-1">














<div
class="content_right">















<div
class="artist_bio_container
clearfix">
















<div
class="artist_bio
short_bio">
















<div
class="artist_bio_inner">

















Without
question
the
most
intelligent,
artistic
rap
group
during
the
1990s,
A
Tribe
Called
Quest
jump-started
and
perfected
the
hip-hop
alternative
to
hardcore
and
gangsta
rap.
In
essence,
they
abandoned
the
macho
posturing
rap
music
had
been
constructed
upon,
and
focused
instead
on
abstract
philosophy
and
message
tracks.
The
&quot;sucka
MC&quot;
theme
had
never
been
completely
ignored
in
hip-hop,
but
Tribe
confronted
numerous
black
issues
--
date
rape,
use
of
the
word
n**ger,
the
trials
and
tribulations
of
the
rap
industry
--
all
of
which
overpowered
the
occasional
game
of
the
dozens.
Just
as
powerful
musically,
Quest
built
upon


















<a
href="/de-la-soul"
class="hash">De
La
Soul's</a>
jazz-rap
revolution,
basing
tracks
around
laid-back
samples
instead
of
the
played-out


















<a
href="/james-brown"
class="hash">James
Brown</a>-fests
which
many
rappers
had
made
a
cottage
industry
by
the
late
'80s.
Comprised
of


















<a
href="/j-period-q-tip"
class="hash">Q-Tip</a>,


















<a
href="/ali-shaheed-muhammad"
class="hash">Ali
Shaheed
Muhammad</a>,
and
Phife,
A
Tribe
Called
Quest
debuted
in
1989
and
released
their
debut
album
one
year
later.
Second
album


















<a
href="/tribe-called-quest/low-end-theory"
class="hash">The
Low
End
Theory</a>
was,
quite
simply,
the
most
consistent
and
flowing
hip-hop
album
ever
recorded,
though
the
trio
moved
closer
to
their
harder
contemporaries
on
1993's


















<a
href="/tribe-called-quest/midnight-marauders"
class="hash">Midnight
Marauders</a>.
A
spot
on
the
1994
Lollapalooza
Tour
showed
their
influence
with
the
alternative
crowd
--
always
a
bedrock
of
A
Tribe
Called
Quest's
support
--
but
the
group
kept
it
real
on
1996's


















<a
href="/tribe-called-quest/beats-rhymes-life"
class="hash">Beats,
Rhymes
and
Life</a>,
a
dedication
to
the
streets
and
the
hip-hop
underground.


















<br
/>

















<br
/>
A
Tribe
Called
Quest
was
formed
in
1988,
though
both


















<a
href="/j-period-q-tip"
class="hash">Q-Tip</a>
(b.
Jonathan
Davis)
and
Phife
(b.
Malik
Taylor)
had
grown
up
together
in
Queens.


















<a
href="/j-period-q-tip"
class="hash">Q-Tip</a>
met
DJ


















<a
href="/ali-shaheed-muhammad"
class="hash">Ali
Shaheed
Muhammad</a>
while
at
high
school
and,
after
being
named
by


















<a
href="/jungle-brothers"
class="hash">the
Jungle
Brothers</a>
(who
attended
the
same
school),
the
trio
began
performing.
A
Tribe
Called
Quest's
recording
debut
came
in
August
1989,
when
their
single,
&quot;Description
of
a
Fool,&quot;
appeared
on
a
tiny
area
label
(though


















<a
href="/j-period-q-tip"
class="hash">Q-Tip</a>
had
previously
guested
on
several
tracks
from


















<a
href="/de-la-soul"
class="hash">De
La
Soul</a>'s


















<a
href="#"
class="hash">3
Feet
High
and
Rising</a>
and
later
appeared
on


















<a
href="/deee-lite"
class="hash">Deee-Lite</a>'s
&quot;Groove
Is
in
the
Heart&quot;).


















<br
/>

















<br
/>
Signed
to
Jive
Records
by
1989,
A
Tribe
Called
Quest
released
their
first
album,


















<a
href="/tribe-called-quest/peoples-instinctive-travels-paths-of-rhythm"
class="hash">People's
Instinctive
Travels
and
the
Paths
of
Rhythm</a>,
one
year
later.
Much
like


















<a
href="/de-la-soul"
class="hash">De
La
Soul</a>,
Tribe
looked
more
to
jazz
as
well
as
'70s
rock
for
their
sample
base
--
&quot;Can
I
Kick
It?&quot;
plundered


















<a
href="/lou-reed-metallica"
class="hash">Lou
Reed's</a>
classic
&quot;Walk
on
the
Wild
Side&quot;
and
made
it
viable
in
a
hip-hop
context.
No
matter
how
solid
their
debut
was,
second
album


















<a
href="/tribe-called-quest/low-end-theory"
class="hash">The
Low
End
Theory</a>
outdid
all
expectations
and
has
held
up
as
perhaps
the
best
hip-hop
LP
of
all
time.


















<br
/>

















<br
/>


















<a
href="/tribe-called-quest/low-end-theory"
class="hash">The
Low
End
Theory</a>
had
included
several
tracks
with
props
to
hip-hop
friends,
and
A
Tribe
Called
Quest
cemented
their
support
of
the
rap
community
with
1993's


















<a
href="/tribe-called-quest/midnight-marauders"
class="hash">Midnight
Marauders</a>.
The
album
cover
and
booklet
insert
included
the
faces
of
more
than
50
rappers
--
including
obvious
choices
such
as


















<a
href="/de-la-soul"
class="hash">De
La
Soul</a>
and


















<a
href="/jungle-brothers"
class="hash">the
Jungle
Brothers</a>
--
as
well
as
mild
surprises
like


















<a
href="/beastie-boys"
class="hash">the
Beastie
Boys</a>,


















<a
href="/ice-t"
class="hash">Ice-T</a>,
and
Heavy
D.
Though
impossible
to
trump
Low
End's
brilliance,
the
LP
offered
several
classics
(including
Tribe's
most
infectious
single
to
date,
&quot;Award
Tour&quot;)
and
a
harder
sound
than
the
first
two
albums.
During
the
summer
of
1994,
A
Tribe
Called
Quest
toured
as
the
obligatory
rap
act
on
the
Lollapalooza
Festival
lineup,
and
spent
a
quiet
1995,
marked
only
by
several
production
jobs
for


















<a
href="/j-period-q-tip"
class="hash">Q-Tip</a>.
Returning
in
1996
with
their
fourth
LP,


















<a
href="/tribe-called-quest/beats-rhymes-life"
class="hash">Beats,
Rhymes
and
Life</a>,
Tribe
showed
signs
of
wear;
it
was
a
good
album,
but
proved
less
striking
than


















<a
href="/tribe-called-quest/low-end-theory"
class="hash">The
Low
End
Theory</a>
or


















<a
href="/tribe-called-quest/midnight-marauders"
class="hash">Midnight
Marauders</a>.
While
touring
in
support
of
1998's


















<a
href="/tribe-called-quest/love-movement"
class="hash">The
Love
Movement</a>,
the
group
announced
their
impending
breakup.
~
John
Bush,
Rovi
















</div>















</div>
















<a
href="#"
class="full_bio_link">full
bio</a>















</div>
